## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics (classical mechanics: nonlinear oscillators)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration, and features are position x, velocity v, and time t, which matches second-order ODE models of (non)linear harmonic oscillators. Typical relationships combine a restoring force term depending on x, damping depending on v, and possibly explicit time-dependent forcing or parametric excitation.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Undamped linear oscillator (Hooke restoring): dv_dt = -c0 * x (small-amplitude mass-spring, conservative)
- Viscous damping only: dv_dt = -c0 * v (free velocity relaxation in a resistive medium)
- Damped linear oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (mass-spring-damper near equilibrium)
- Constant + linear bias (equilibrium shift): dv_dt = c0 - c1 * x - c2 * v (gravity/bias force plus spring-damper)
- Harmonically driven oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (external periodic forcing)
- Pendulum-like restoring (geometric nonlinearity): dv_dt = -c0 * sin(c1 * x) - c2 * v (finite-angle oscillations with damping)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Quintic stiffness extension: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * x**5 - c3 * v (strongly nonlinear springs, buckling-like behavior)
- Nonlinear damping (cubic drag): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * v**3 (aerodynamic/velocity-dependent dissipation)
- Van der Pol (self-excited oscillator): dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (negative damping at small |x|, limit cycle)
- Liénard-type oscillator (general nonlinear damping + restoring): dv_dt = -c0 * (c1 + c2 * x**2) * v - (c3 * x + c4 * x**3) (broad class capturing amplitude-dependent damping and stiffness)
- Parametrically excited oscillator: dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (time-varying stiffness, Mathieu-type resonance)
- Dry friction approximation: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * tanh(c3 * v) (Coulomb-like friction smoothed near v=0)
- Rational softening saturation of restoring force: dv_dt = -c0 * x / (1 + c1 * x**2) - c2 * v (restoring force saturates at large |x|)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative (energy-preserving) oscillator behavior often implies dv_dt depends on x only (no v, no t), i.e., dv_dt ≈ -dU/dx with U(x) even for symmetric potentials.
- Linearization near equilibrium typically yields dv_dt ≈ -c0 * x - c1 * v; deviations from this suggest nonlinear stiffness (x**3, sin(c*x)) or nonlinear damping (v**3, x**2*v).
- Odd restoring forces (terms like x, x**3, sin(c*x)) indicate symmetric potentials; the presence of even-in-x terms can indicate asymmetry or bias/tilt in the potential.
- Amplitude-dependent frequency is commonly captured by adding cubic/quintic stiffness terms (x**3, x**5); hardening vs softening corresponds to the sign of those coefficients.
- Self-excitation/limit cycles are suggested by damping that changes sign with amplitude, e.g., (1 - c*x**2)*v (negative damping at small amplitude, positive at large).
- Explicit periodic dependence on t in additive forcing (sin(c*t), cos(c*t)) indicates driven oscillations; periodic dependence multiplying x indicates parametric excitation and possible resonance bands.
- Strong dissipation or drag-limited motion often produces nonlinear velocity dependence (v*Abs(v), v**3, tanh(c*v)), which alters decay rate and waveform shape.
- Frictional effects near v = 0 can create non-smooth dynamics; smooth surrogates (tanh(c*v)) can approximate stick-slip transitions in regression-friendly form.

I need to analyze each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT numerical expression:**
`-1.85799332865866*x*(0.0355398482733264*Abs(v)**0.333333333333333 + 1) - 1.85799332865866*x - 1.85799332865866*x*exp(-Abs(x)) + 0.681325524225947*sin(t)`

Let me expand this:
`-1.85799332865866*0.0355398482733264*x*Abs(v)**0.333333333333333 - 1.85799332865866*x - 1.85799332865866*x - 1.85799332865866*x*exp(-Abs(x)) + 0.681325524225947*sin(t)`

Simplifying:
`-0.06601...*x*Abs(v)**(1/3) - 3.71598665731732*x - 1.85799332865866*x*exp(-Abs(x)) + 0.681325524225947*sin(t)`

Key structural components of GT:
1. A term proportional to `x*Abs(v)^(1/3)` — depends on both x and v with fractional power of |v|
2. A linear term in `x`
3. A term `x*exp(-Abs(x))` — note this involves `Abs(x)`, not just `x`
4. A `sin(t)` term

The critical features are:
- **`x*exp(-|x|)`**: This is NOT the same as `x*exp(cx)` for any constant c, because `exp(-|x|)` is not `exp(cx)` (|x| ≠ ±x for all x).
- **`x*|v|^(1/3)`**: This requires a coupling between x and a fractional power of |v|.

Let me now check each candidate:

**Key observation about `x*exp(-|x|)`:** Since x takes both positive and negative values, `exp(-|x|)` cannot be written as `exp(c*x)` for any constant c. The function `exp(-|x|)` is even, while `exp(cx)` is neither even nor odd. So any candidate using `exp(c*x)` instead of `exp(-Abs(x))` **cannot match** the GT term `x*exp(-|x|)`.

**Key observation about `x*|v|^(1/3)`:** This requires explicit dependence on v in a specific nonlinear way. Candidates without v-dependence (or with wrong v-dependence) cannot match.

Let me quickly categorize:

**Candidates without any v-dependence AND using exp(c*x):** These miss both the `x*|v|^(1/3)` term and the `x*exp(-|x|)` term. This eliminates candidates: 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6, 9, 12, 13, 14, 15, 16, 21, 23, 24, 25, 27, 28, 30, 31, 33, 34, 35, 36, 37, 38, 42, 43, 44, 46.

**Candidates with v-dependence but using exp(c*x):** Still can't match `x*exp(-|x|)`. This eliminates: 7, 8, 10, 11, 17, 18, 19, 20, 22, 26, 29, 32, 39, 40, 41, 45, 47, 48, 49, 50.

Since `x*exp(-|x|)` cannot be represented by `exp(c*x)` (because x takes both signs), and none of the candidates contain `exp(-Abs(x))` or equivalent, **no candidate can match the GT**.

Let me verify candidate 40 specifically: `c0 + c1*x**5 + c2*exp(c3*x) + c4*sin(c5*t + c6) + c7*x*(c8 + v)**c9 + x**2` — has `x*(c8+v)^c9` which could approximate `x*|v|^(1/3)` only if c8=0 and we ignore the absolute value issue. Still uses `exp(c3*x)` not `exp(-|x|)`.

After careful analysis, no candidate matches.
